# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Task Information

**Task ID**: rust_ml_computer_vision_expert_054_architectural_understanding_expert_01

## Task Title

Architectural Analysis for Microservice Extraction in VisuTility Orchestrator

## Description

VisuTility Orchestrator is a complex, monolithic Rust application for managing computer vision MLOps pipelines. Due to its success, the business wants to offer its powerful experiment tracking capabilities as a standalone, cloud-native product. This requires extracting the relevant logic into a new, independent microservice. The current codebase is large and complex, with module names obfuscated, requiring deep analysis to untangle dependencies. The task is to perform the initial architectural analysis to plan this extraction.

## Your Task

You are a senior software architect. Your goal is to analyze the 'VisuTility Orchestrator' codebase and produce a plan for extracting the 'experiment_tracking' feature into a separate microservice. You must not write any new code, but provide a detailed architectural report.

Your report must contain four sections:

1.  **Core Component Identification:** Identify the primary Rust modules (e.g., `src/module_XX.txt`) that constitute the core logic for experiment tracking. This includes managing experiments, runs, logging metrics, parameters, and artifacts.

2.  **Dependency Analysis:** Create a dependency map for the identified core components. This map should detail:
    *   **Internal Dependencies:** Which other modules within the monolith do the core experiment tracking modules depend on (e.g., database connectors, shared data structures, configuration loaders)?
    *   **External Consumers:** Which other modules in the monolith consume the services of the experiment tracking components (e.g., model training or hyperparameter tuning modules that need to log their results)?

3.  **Proposed Service API:** Define a high-level, language-agnostic RESTful API for the new 'Experiment Tracking' microservice. The API should expose all necessary functionalities currently provided internally. Specify the resources, endpoints, HTTP methods, and expected request/response payloads (in brief).

4.  **Refactoring Plan:** List the specific modules within the remaining monolith that will require modification to use the new microservice API instead of the current internal calls. For each module, briefly describe the nature of the change required.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this task systematically:

1.  **Keyword-based Search:** Perform a global search across all `src/*.txt` files for keywords related to experiment tracking, such as `experiment`, `run`, `metric`, `parameter`, `log_metric`, `log_param`, `artifact`, `start_run`, `end_run`.
2.  **Module Triaging:** Analyze the search results to identify a small set of modules with the highest concentration and relevance of these keywords. These are the likely core components.
3.  **Dependency Tracing (Internal):** For each identified core module, inspect its `use` statements and function calls to other modules. This will reveal its dependencies on shared utilities like database clients (`db::`), configuration (`config::`), or common data types (`types::`).
4.  **Dependency Tracing (External):** Use IDE tools or command-line searches (like `grep`) to find all usages of the public functions, structs, and traits defined in the core experiment tracking modules. The files containing these usages are the 'External Consumers'.
5.  **API Synthesis:** Based on the functions exposed by the core modules (e.g., `create_experiment`, `log_metric_to_run`, `get_run_details`), synthesize a logical, resource-oriented RESTful API. Common patterns would be `POST /runs` to create, `PATCH /runs/{id}` to update (e.g., log metrics), and `GET /runs/{id}` to retrieve.
6.  **Consolidation:** Compile the findings into the four requested sections. The 'Refactoring Plan' would be directly derived from the list of 'External Consumers' identified in step 4.

## Evaluation Criteria

- {'name': 'Correctness of Core Component Identification', 'description': 'Agent correctly identifies a plausible set of modules responsible for experiment tracking, based on code analysis.'}
- {'name': 'Accuracy of Dependency Mapping', 'description': 'Agent correctly identifies both key modules that are depended upon (e.g., DB, config) and key modules that are consumers (e.g., training, tuning).'}
- {'name': 'Quality and Completeness of API Design', 'description': 'The proposed API is well-structured, RESTful, and covers the essential functionalities of creating runs and logging data. The design is logical and practical.'}
- {'name': 'Viability of Refactoring Plan', 'description': 'The agent correctly identifies the modules that need to be refactored and accurately describes the nature of the required changes (i.e., replacing internal calls with API calls).'}
- {'name': 'Clarity of Rationale', 'description': 'The agent provides clear justifications for its conclusions, referencing evidence from the codebase to support its identification of modules and dependencies.'}

     2→//! module_12 – Hyperparameter Tuning & Experiment Tracking
     3→//!
     4→//! This module lives in the “Model Ops” layer of VisuTility Orchestrator.

     6→//!  1. Strategy-based hyper-parameter tuning (currently Random Search,

     1→```rust
     2→//! src/module_25.rs
     3→//!
     4→//! Experiment-tracking and hyper-parameter tuning utilities used by
     5→//! VisuTility Orchestrator’s Model-Ops layer.
     6→//!
     7→//! The module demonstrates a concrete implementation of several of the
     8→//! architectural patterns mentioned in the project documentation:
     9→//!   • Strategy Pattern: `HyperParamTuner` selects among tuning strategies
    10→//!     (`GridSearchTuner`, `RandomSearchTuner`, …).
    11→//!   • Observer Pattern: `TuningSubject` notifies `TuningObserver`s about new
    12→//!     trial results so that other subsystems (alerting, dashboards, etc.)
    13→//!     can react in real-time.
    14→//!   • Factory Pattern: `TrackerFactory` picks the correct
    15→//!     `ExperimentTracker` backend.
    16→//!
    17→//! All public types are designed to remain stable across minor releases so
    18→//! that external micro-services can rely on them via semantic versioning.
    19→
    20→use async_trait::async_trait;
    21→use rand::{seq::SliceRandom, Rng};
    22→use reqwest::Client;
    23→use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
    24→use serde_json::json;
    25→use std::{
    26→    collections::HashMap,
    27→    fs::{File, OpenOptions},
    28→    io::{BufWriter, Write},
    29→    path::PathBuf,
    30→    sync::{Arc, Mutex},
    31→};
    32→use thiserror::Error;
    33→use tokio::sync::broadcast;
    34→
    35→/// Domain-level error type.
    36→#[derive(Debug, Error)]

83-assistanttext-
I have completed the architectural analysis for extracting the experiment tracking feature from the VisuTility Orchestrator monolith. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Analysis Summary

### 1. Core Components Identified
The experiment tracking functionality is distributed across 7 primary modules:
- **module_12.txt** - Main in-memory `ExperimentTracker` with run management
- **module_25.txt** - `ExperimentTracker` trait + Factory pattern for tracker backends
- **module_20.txt** - `HyperparameterRunner` integrating with trackers
- **module_71.txt** - SQLite-backed persistence layer
- **module_55.txt** - Observer pattern with `ExperimentEvent`/`ExperimentObserver`
- **module_48.txt** - JSONL file-based tracker implementation
- **module_76.txt** - Monitoring integration with experiment logging

### 2. Dependency Map
**Internal dependencies**: config.txt (configuration), utils.txt (event bus, error types), constants.txt (feature flags), plus external crates (serde, tokio, rusqlite, reqwest)

**External consumers**: module_43 (ModelMonitor), module_54 (TuningCoordinator), module_76 (RetrainTrigger), module_77 (hyperparameter tuning), module_20 (HyperparameterRunner)

### 3. Proposed REST API
A resource-oriented API covering:
- `/experiments` - CRUD for experiments
- `/experiments/{id}/runs` - Run lifecycle management
- `/experiments/{id}/runs/{id}/metrics` - Metric logging
- `/experiments/{id}/runs/{id}/params` - Parameter logging
- `/experiments/{id}/runs/{id}/artifacts` - Artifact storage

### 4. Refactoring Plan
10 modules need modification to replace internal tracker calls with HTTP client calls to the new microservice, including creation of a thin `ExperimentTrackingClient` that implements the existing `ExperimentTracker` trait for backward compatibility.

The comple

The module demonstrates a concrete implementation of several of the\n//! architectural patterns mentioned in the project documentation:\n//!   \u2022 Strategy Pattern: `HyperParamTuner` selects among tuning strategies\n//!     (`GridSearchTuner`, `RandomSearchTuner`, \u2026).\n//!   \u2022 Observer Pattern: `TuningSubject` notifies `TuningObserver`s about new\n//!     trial results so that other subsystems (alerting, dashboards, etc.)\n//!     can react in real-time.\n//!   \u2022 Factory Pattern: `TrackerFactory` picks the correct\n//!     `ExperimentTracker` backend.\n//!\n//! All public types are designed to remain stable across minor releases so\n//! that external micro-services can rely on them via semantic versioning.\n\nuse async_trait::async_trait;\nuse rand::{seq::SliceRandom, Rng};\nuse reqwest::Client;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse serde_json::json;\nuse std::{\n    collections::HashMap,\n    fs::{File, OpenOptions},\n    io::{BufWriter, Write},\n    path::PathBuf,\n    sync::{Arc, Mutex},\n};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tokio::sync::broadcast;\n\n/// Domain-level error type.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum OrchestratorError {\n    #[error(\"IO error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"HTTP error: {0}\")]\n    Http(#[from] reqwest::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"Broadcast channel error: {0}\")]\n    BroadcastRecv(#[from] broadcast::error::RecvError),\n\n    #[error(\"Unknown error: {0}\")]\n    Other(String),\n}\n\n/// Represents a concrete hyper-parameter value.\n///\n/// We purposefully remain JSON-compatible so that values can be directly\n/// serialized for experiment tracking.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(untagged)]\npub enum HyperParamValue {\n    Int(i64),\n    Float(f64),\n    Text(String),\n    Bool(bool),\n}\n\n/// Full specification of a single trial.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct Trial {\n    pub id: u64,\n    pub params: HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n    pub metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n}\n\n/// Trait describing the capabilities of an experiment-tracker backend.\n///\n/// Implementations must be easy to swap at runtime.\n///\n/// NOTE: This trait is async because some backends perform network IO.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait ExperimentTracker: Send + Sync {\n    async fn log_trial(&self, trial: &Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError>;\n}\n\n/// Simple JSON-Lines file tracker.\n///\n/// Each trial is appended as a single JSON object on its own line.\npub struct FileTracker {\n    /// Lazily-opened file handle wrapped in a Mutex for thread-safety.\n    file: Arc<Mutex<BufWriter<File>>>,\n}\n\nimpl FileTracker {\n    pub fn new<P: Into<PathBuf>>(path: P) -> Result<Self, OrchestratorError> {\n        let file = OpenOptions::new()\n            .create(true)\n            .append(true)\n            .open(path.into())?;\n        Ok(Self {\n            file: Arc::new(Mutex::new(BufWriter::new(file))),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl ExperimentTracker for FileTracker {\n    async fn log_trial(&self, trial: &Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        let mut writer = self.file.lock().unwrap();\n        serde_json::to_writer(&mut *writer, trial)?;\n        writer.write_all(b\"\\n\")?;\n        writer.flush()?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// HTTP tracker that POSTs a JSON payload to a remote endpoint.\npub struct HttpTracker {\n    endpoint: String,\n    client: Client,\n}\n\nimpl HttpTracker {\n    pub fn new<S: Into<String>>(endpoint: S) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            endpoint: endpoint.into(),\n            client: Client::new(),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl ExperimentTracker for HttpTracker {\n    async fn log_trial(&self, trial: &Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        self.client\n            .post(&self.endpoint)\n            .json(trial)\n            .send()\n            .await?\n            .error_for_status()?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Factory pattern: pick an `ExperimentTracker` based on a declarative config.\npub enum TrackerFactory {}\n\nimpl TrackerFactory {\n    pub fn build(config: &TrackerConfig) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExperimentTracker>, OrchestratorError> {\n        match config {\n            TrackerConfig::File { path } => Ok(Arc::new(FileTracker::new(path)?)),\n            TrackerConfig::Http { endpoint } => Ok(Arc::new(HttpTracker::new(endpoint))),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Minimal config enum that can be deserialized from JSON/YAML/TOML.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n#[serde(tag = \"type\", rename_all = \"snake_case\")]\npub enum TrackerConfig {\n    File { path: PathBuf },\n    Http { endpoint: String },\n}\n\n/// Observer pattern: observers react to new trial events.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait TuningObserver: Send + Sync {\n    async fn on_new_trial(&self, trial: &Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError>;\n}\n\n/// The subject that notifies all registered observers.\npub struct TuningSubject {\n    tx: broadcast::Sender<Trial>,\n}\n\nimpl TuningSubject {\n    pub fn new(buffer: usize) -> Self {\n        let (tx, _) = broadcast::channel(buffer);\n        Self { tx }\n    }\n\n    pub fn observer_stream(&self) -> broadcast::Receiver<Trial> {\n        self.tx.subscribe()\n    }\n\n    pub fn notify(&self, trial: Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        // If there are no observers, we ignore the error.\n        let _ = self.tx.send(trial);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Any hyper-parameter tuner must implement this trait.\n/// Strategies (grid search, random search, Bayesian, \u2026) can be hot-swapped.\n#[async_trait]\npub trait HyperParamTuner {\n    async fn run(\n        &mut self,\n        tracker: Arc<dyn ExperimentTracker>,\n        subject: Arc<TuningSubject>,\n    ) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError>;\n}\n\n/// Deterministic grid-search tuner.\npub struct GridSearchTuner {\n    /// Each parameter maps to a list of possible discrete values.\n    /// Example: {\"lr\": [0.1, 0.01], \"batch\": [16, 32]}\n    param_grid: HashMap<String, Vec<HyperParamValue>>,\n    max_trials: Option<usize>,\n    current_trial_id: u64,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(\n        param_grid: HashMap<String, Vec<HyperParamValue>>,\n        max_trials: Option<usize>,\n    ) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            param_grid,\n            max_trials,\n            current_trial_id: 0,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Helper that expands the grid into the Cartesian product.\n    fn expand_grid(\n        &self,\n    ) -> Vec<HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>> {\n        fn helper(\n            keys: &[String],\n            idx: usize,\n            grid: &HashMap<String, Vec<HyperParamValue>>,\n            acc: &mut HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n            out: &mut Vec<HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>>,\n        ) {\n            if idx == keys.len() {\n                out.push(acc.clone());\n                return;\n            }\n            let key = &keys[idx];\n            if let Some(values) = grid.get(key) {\n                for val in values {\n                    acc.insert(key.clone(), val.clone());\n                    helper(keys, idx + 1, grid, acc, out);\n                    acc.remove(key);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n\n        let keys: Vec<String> = self.param_grid.keys().cloned().collect();\n        let mut out = Vec::new();\n        helper(&keys, 0, &self.param_grid, &mut HashMap::new(), &mut out);\n        out\n    }\n\n    /// Fake metric evaluator. In reality, this would invoke a real training\n    /// job and return its validation score. For demo purposes we sample a\n    /// random metric to keep the code fully functional without dependencies\n    /// on heavy ML frameworks.\n    async fn evaluate(\n        &mut self,\n        params: &HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n    ) -> Result<HashMap<String, f64>, OrchestratorError> {\n        let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();\n        // Pretend lower is better for \"loss\".\n        Ok(HashMap::from([(\"loss\".to_string(), rng.gen::<f64>())]))\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl HyperParamTuner for GridSearchTuner {\n    async fn run(\n        &mut self,\n        tracker: Arc<dyn ExperimentTracker>,\n        subject: Arc<TuningSubject>,\n    ) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        let combos = self.expand_grid();\n        let limit = self.max_trials.unwrap_or(combos.len());\n        for params in combos.into_iter().take(limit) {\n            let metrics = self.evaluate(&params).await?;\n            let trial = Trial {\n                id: self.current_trial_id,\n                params,\n                metrics,\n            };\n            self.current_trial_id += 1;\n\n            tracker.log_trial(&trial).await?;\n            subject.notify(trial)?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Non-deterministic random-search tuner.\npub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n    param_space: HashMap<String, Vec<HyperParamValue>>,\n    num_trials: usize,\n    current_trial_id: u64,\n}\n\nimpl RandomSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(param_space: HashMap<String, Vec<HyperParamValue>>, num_trials: usize) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            param_space,\n            num_trials,\n            current_trial_id: 0,\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn sample_params(&self) -> HashMap<String, HyperParamValue> {\n        let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();\n        self.param_space\n            .iter()\n            .map(|(k, v)| {\n                let choice = v.choose(&mut rng).unwrap().clone();\n                (k.clone(), choice)\n            })\n            .collect()\n    }\n\n    async fn evaluate(\n        &mut self,\n        params: &HashMap<String, HyperParamValue>,\n    ) -> Result<HashMap<String, f64>, OrchestratorError> {\n        let mut rng = rand::thread_rng();\n        Ok(HashMap::from([(\"accuracy\".to_string(), rng.gen::<f64>())]))\n    }\n}\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl HyperParamTuner for RandomSearchTuner {\n    async fn run(\n        &mut self,\n        tracker: Arc<dyn ExperimentTracker>,\n        subject: Arc<TuningSubject>,\n    ) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        for _ in 0..self.num_trials {\n            let params = self.sample_params();\n            let metrics = self.evaluate(&params).await?;\n            let trial = Trial {\n                id: self.current_trial_id,\n                params,\n                metrics,\n            };\n            self.current_trial_id += 1;\n\n            tracker.log_trial(&trial).await?;\n            subject.notify(trial)?;\n        }\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example observer that prints new trials to stdout.\n/// In production this could push to Prometheus, GUI dashboards, etc.\npub struct StdoutObserver;\n\n#[async_trait]\nimpl TuningObserver for StdoutObserver {\n    async fn on_new_trial(&self, trial: &Trial) -> Result<(), OrchestratorError> {\n        println!(\n            \"\ud83e\uddea New trial #{} | params={} | metrics={}\",\n            trial.id,\n            json!(trial.params),\n            json!(trial.metrics)\n        );\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n\n/// Spawns  observer: Arc<O>,\n) {\n    tokio::spawn(async move {\n        let mut rx = subject.observer_stream();\n        loop {\n            match rx.recv().await {\n                Ok(trial) => {\n                    if let Err(e) = observer.on_new_trial(&trial).await {\n                        eprintln!(\"Observer error: {e}\");\n                    }\n                }\n                Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Closed) => break,\n                Err(broadcast::error::RecvError::Lagged(_)) => continue,\n            }\n        }\n    });\n}\n\n/// Entrypoint used by integration tests or CLIs.\n///\n/// NOT called automatically by library consumers.\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use std::env::temp_dir;\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn     "content": "```rust\n/*!\nModule 71 \u2013 Adaptive hyper-parameter tuning & experiment tracking\n\nThis module provides a production-grade implementation of:\n\n* Strategy Pattern \u2013 multiple `HyperparameterTuner` strategies at runtime\n* Observer Pattern  \u2013 `TrainingObserver` that receives callbacks from the\n  model-training engine and feeds metrics back into the tuner\n* Experiment tracking \u2013 light-weight SQLite persistence backed by `rusqlite`\n  for auditability\n\nThe module is self-contained and does not perform the actual model training.\nInstead, it exposes stable, async-friendly APIs that the higher-level\n`Model Ops` layer can call to obtain hyper-parameters and report training\nresults.\n\nThe public surface area is intentionally small so that it can be consumed\nfrom other language bindings (FFI), gRPC layers, or CLI tooling.\n*/\n\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\nuse std::path::{Path, PathBuf};\nuse std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\n\nuse anyhow::{Context, Result};\nuse chrono::{DateTime, Utc};\nuse log::{debug, error, info, warn};\nuse rand::seq::SliceRandom;\nuse rand::{thread_rng, Rng};\nuse rusqlite::{params, Connection};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n/// Common alias for hyper-parameter name/value mapping.\npub type HyperParams = HashMap<String, f64>;\n\n/// Strategy pattern: A tuner is responsible for suggesting the next set of\n/// hyper-parameters *and* ingesting the resulting score so that it can adapt\n/// its internal search.\n///\n/// Implementors must be `Send + Sync` so that the search can be distributed\n/// across threads or processes.\n///\n/// NOTE: The tuner does *not* execute the training job.  That responsibility\n/// lies with the `Model Ops` layer.  The tuner is also side-effect free\u2013\u2013\n/// apart from internal bookkeeping.\npub trait HyperparameterTuner: Send + Sync {\n    /// Suggest the next configuration to evaluate.\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams>;\n\n    /// Report the evaluation metric (e.g. accuracy, loss) for a previously\n    /// suggested configuration.  Implementations may choose to ignore the\n    /// score when the configuration is unknown.\n    fn report_result(&mut self, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64);\n\n    /// Human-readable name; useful for telemetry & debugging.\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str;\n}\n\n/// A simple grid-search tuner that exhaustively evaluates the Cartesian\n/// product of discrete candidate values.\n///\n/// Useful for deterministic sweeps when the search space is small.\npub struct GridSearchTuner {\n    grid: Vec<HyperParams>,\n    cursor: usize,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>>) -> Self {\n        // Compute Cartesian product\n        let mut grid: Vec<HyperParams> = vec![];\n        Self::cartesian_product(\n            &mut grid,\n            &mut HyperParams::new(),\n            &candidates.into_iter().collect::<Vec<_>>(),\n            0,\n        );\n        info!(\"GridSearch initialized with {} configurations\", grid.len());\n        Self { grid, cursor: 0 }\n    }\n\n    fn cartesian_product(\n        acc: &mut Vec<HyperParams>,\n        current: &mut HyperParams,\n        items: &[(String, Vec<f64>)],\n        idx: usize,\n    ) {\n        if idx == items.len() {\n            acc.push(current.clone());\n            return;\n        }\n\n        let (ref key, ref values) = items[idx];\n        for v in values {\n            current.insert(key.clone(), *v);\n            Self::cartesian_product(acc, current, items, idx + 1);\n        }\n        current.remove(key);\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for GridSearchTuner {\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.cursor >= self.grid.len() {\n            None\n        } else {\n            let params = self.grid[self.cursor].clone();\n            self.cursor += 1;\n            Some(params)\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn report_result(&mut self, _params: &HyperParams, _metric: f64) {\n        // grid search is stateless; nothing to do.\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"GridSearchTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/// Random search tuner that samples uniformly from user-supplied ranges.\n/// Each range is inclusive.\n///\n/// NOTE: For continuous variables, the range is treated as continuous;\n/// for discrete variables, the caller can pass equal min==max to achieve\n/// deterministic behavior.\npub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n    ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>,\n    max_trials: usize,\n    trials: usize,\n    history: Vec<(HyperParams, f64)>,\n}\n\nimpl RandomSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>, max_trials: usize) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            ranges,\n            max_trials,\n            trials: 0,\n            history: Vec::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn random_sample(&self) -> HyperParams {\n        let mut rng = thread_rng();\n        self.ranges\n            .iter()\n            .map(|(k, (min, max))| (k.clone(), rng.gen_range(*min..=*max)))\n            .collect()\n    }\n}\n\nimpl HyperparameterTuner for RandomSearchTuner {\n    fn suggest(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.trials >= self.max_trials {\n            None\n        } else {\n            self.trials += 1;\n            Some(self.random_sample())\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn report_result(&mut self, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64) {\n        self.history.push((params.clone(), metric));\n    }\n\n    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {\n        \"RandomSearchTuner\"\n    }\n}\n\n/// Factory pattern: build tuners dynamically based on a string identifier.\n/// This allows runtime configuration via CLI, YAML, or remote control plane.\npub enum TunerFactory;\n\nimpl TunerFactory {\n    pub fn make_grid_search(candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>>) -> Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner> {\n        Box::new(GridSearchTuner::new(candidates))\n    }\n\n    pub fn make_random_search(\n        ranges: HashMap<String, (f64, f64)>,\n        max_trials: usize,\n    ) -> Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner> {\n        Box::new(RandomSearchTuner::new(ranges, max_trials))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Observer pattern \u2013 The model-training engine emits `TrainingEvent`s that\n/// observers can subscribe to.  The tuner implementation itself can be an\n/// observer in order to implement adaptive search algorithms such as Bayesian\n/// optimization, however, we keep them decoupled so that multiple observers\n/// (e.g. loggers, alerting) can co-exist.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub enum TrainingEvent {\n    EpochStart { epoch: u32 },\n    EpochEnd {\n        epoch: u32,\n        metrics: HashMap<String, f64>,\n    },\n    TrainingFinish {\n        best_metric: f64,\n        best_params: HyperParams,\n    },\n}\n\n/// Observer trait.\npub trait TrainingObserver: Send + Sync {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: &TrainingEvent);\n}\n\n/// Default implementation that feeds back the final metric to the tuner.\npub struct TunerObserver {\n    tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>>,\n}\n\nimpl TunerObserver {\n    pub fn new(tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>>) -> Self {\n        Self { tuner }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TrainingObserver for TunerObserver {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: &TrainingEvent) {\n        if let TrainingEvent::TrainingFinish {\n            best_metric,\n            best_params,\n        } = event\n        {\n            if let Ok(mut tuner) = self.tuner.lock() {\n                tuner.report_result(best_params, *best_metric);\n            } else {\n                error!(\"Unable to lock tuner mutex in observer\");\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Lightweight experiment tracking backed by SQLite.\n/// Production deployments can replace this with a more\n/// sophisticated store (Postgres, Influx, etc.) via\n/// feature flags without changing the public API.\n#[derive(Debug)]\npub struct ExperimentTracker {\n    db_path: PathBuf,\n    conn: Connection,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ExperimentRecord {\n    pub id: i64,\n    pub timestamp: DateTime<Utc>,\n    pub tuner_name: String,\n    pub params: HyperParams,\n    pub metric: f64,\n}\n\nimpl ExperimentTracker {\n    /// Create a new tracker with the given file path.\n    pub fn new<P: AsRef<Path>>(db_path: P) -> Result<Self> {\n        let conn = Connection::open(&db_path)\n            .with_context(|| format!(\"opening experiments db {:?}\", db_path.as_ref()))?;\n\n        let tracker = Self {\n            db_path: db_path.as_ref().to_path_buf(),\n            conn,\n        };\n\n        tracker.init_schema()?;\n        Ok(tracker)\n    }\n\n    fn init_schema(&self) -> Result<()> {\n        self.conn.execute_batch(\n            \"\n            CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS experiments (\n                id          INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT,\n                timestamp   TEXT NOT NULL,\n                tuner_name  TEXT NOT NULL,\n                params      BLOB NOT NULL,\n                metric      REAL NOT NULL\n            );\n            \",\n        )?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Persist an experiment record.\n    pub fn log_record(&self, tuner_name: &str, params: &HyperParams, metric: f64) -> Result<i64> {\n        let timestamp: DateTime<Utc> = Utc::now();\n        let params_blob = serde_json::to_vec(params).context(\"serializing hyperparams\")?;\n\n        self.conn.execute(\n            \"\n            INSERT INTO experiments (timestamp, tuner_name, params, metric)\n            VALUES (?1, ?2, ?3, ?4);\n            \",\n            params![\n                timestamp.to_rfc3339(),\n                tuner_name,\n                params_blob,\n                metric\n            ],\n        )?;\n\n        Ok(self.conn.last_insert_rowid())\n    }\n\n    /// Retrieve all experiments for auditing or analytics.\n    pub fn all_records(&self) -> Result<Vec<ExperimentRecord>> {\n        let mut stmt = self.conn.prepare(\n            \"\n            SELECT id, timestamp, tuner_name, params, metric\n            FROM experiments\n            ORDER BY id ASC;\n            \",\n        )?;\n\n        let iter = stmt.query_map([], |row| {\n            let params_blob: Vec<u8> = row.get(3)?;\n            let params: HyperParams = serde_json::from_slice(&params_blob)\n                .map_err(|e| rusqlite::Error::FromSqlConversionFailure(3, rusqlite::types::Type::Blob, Box::new(e)))?;\n\n            Ok(ExperimentRecord {\n                id: row.get(0)?,\n                timestamp: DateTime::parse_from_rfc3339(&row.get::<_, String>(1)?)\n                    .map(|dt| dt.with_timezone(&Utc))\n                    .map_err(|e| rusqlite::Error::FromSqlConversionFailure(1, rusqlite::types::Type::Text, Box::new(e)))?,\n                tuner_name: row.get(2)?,\n                params,\n                metric: row.get(4)?,\n            })\n        })?;\n\n        let mut out = Vec::new();\n        for rec in iter {\n            out.push(rec?);\n        }\n        Ok(out)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example of orchestrating an end-to-end hyper-parameter tuning session.\n/// The function is *sync* for brevity but can be made async using\n/// `tokio::task::spawn_blocking` or similar.\n///\n/// NOTE: This is *not* executed automatically; it serves as a reference\n/// implementation for higher-level orchestration code.\npub fn run_hpo_session() -> Result<()> {\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Create the tuner (here: grid search)\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    let mut candidates: HashMap<String, Vec<f64>> = HashMap::new();\n    candidates.insert(\"learning_rate\".into(), vec![0.01, 0.001]);\n    candidates.insert(\"dropout\".into(), vec![0.1, 0.2, 0.3]);\n\n    let tuner: Arc<Mutex<Box<dyn HyperparameterTuner>>> =\n        Arc::new(Mutex::new(TunerFactory::make_grid_search(candidates)));\n\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Initialize experiment tracker\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    let tracker = ExperimentTracker::new(\"experiments.db\")?;\n\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    // Main loop\n    // ------------------------------------------\n    loop {\n        let next_params = {\n            let mut tuner = tuner.lock().expect(\"tuner lock poisoned\");\n            tuner.suggest()\n        };\n\n        let Some(params) = next_params else {\n            info!(\"Hyper-parameter search complete.\");\n            break;\n        };\n\n        // ------------------------------------------------------------------\n        // >>>>  In the real system, `train_model()` would kick off an *async*\n        // >>>>  training job, possibly on a GPU worker pool and stream back\n        // >>>>  metrics over a channel.  For demonstration, we simulate a\n        // >>>>  random metric here.\n        // ------------------------------------------------------------------\n        let simulated_metric: f64 = thread_rng().gen_range(0.7..0.99);\n\n        // Feed the result back into the tuner *and* log it to the tracker.\n        {\n            let mut tuner_locked = tuner.lock().expect(\"tuner lock poisoned\");\n            tuner_locked.report_result(&params, simulated_metric);\n        }\n\n        tracker\n            .log_record(\"GridSearchTuner\", &params, simulated_metric)\n            .context(\"logging experiment\")?;\n\n        debug!(\n            \"Evaluated {:?} -> metric = {:.4}\",\n            &params, simulated_metric\n        );\n    }\n\n    Ok(())\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod (\"batch_size\".to_string(), (16.0, 128.0)),\n        ]);\n\n        let mut tuner = RandomSearchTuner::new(ranges, 5);\n        let p1 = tuner.suggest().unwrap();\n        tuner.report_result(&p1, 0.92);\n        assert_eq!(tuner.trials, 1);\n        assert_eq!(tuner.history.len(), 1);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_grid_search_exhaustive() {\n        let mut can = HashMap::new();\n        can.insert(\"a\".into(), vec![1.0, 2.0]);\n        can.insert(\"b\".into(), vec![10.0]);\n\n        let mut tuner = GridSearchTuner::new(can);\n        assert!(tuner.suggest().is_some());\n        assert!(tuner.suggest().is_some());\n        assert!(tuner.suggest().is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_experiment_tracker_persistence() -> Result<()> {\n        let tmp = &params, 0.5)?;\n        let records = tracker.all_records()?;\n        assert_eq!(records.len(), 1);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```",

This module contains the implementation of the Strategy\u2010based hyper-parameter\n//! tuner as well as a lightweight Observer for experiment tracking.  Although\n//! the production project offers many more knobs, this file provides a realistic\n//! slice that can be embedded directly into the VisuTility Orchestrator.\n//!\n//! Architectural Patterns Demonstrated\n//! * Strategy Pattern    \u2013 `TunerStrategy` trait + concrete tuners\n//! * Factory  Pattern    \u2013 `TunerFactory` for late-bound instantiation\n//! * Observer Pattern    \u2013 `ExperimentEvent`  + `ExperimentObserver`\n//! * Pipeline  Pattern    \u2013 `run_hyperparameter_tuning` async pipeline\n//!\n//! TrainFailure(String),\n    #[error(\"invalid hyper-parameter space: {0}\")]\n    InvalidSpace(String),\n    #[error(\"internal error: {0}\")]\n    Internal(String),\n}\n\n// ------------------------- Trainable Model Abstraction -----------------------\n/// A minimal contract that every model inside VisuTility needs to implement\n/// in order to participate in automated tuning.\npub trait Trainable: Send + Sync + Debug + 'static {\n    /// User-level hyper-parameter type.\n    type HyperParams: Serialize + for<'de> Deserialize<'de> + Send + Sync + Clone + Debug;\n    /// Metric returned by evaluation.\n    type Metric: PartialOrd + Copy + Debug;\n\n    /// Create a new model instance with the supplied hyper-parameters.\n    fn new(params: &Self::HyperParams) -> Result<Self, TuningError>\n    where\n        Self: Sized;\n\n    /// Train the model on given data split.\n    fn train(&mut self, dataset: DatasetView) -> Result<(), TuningError>;\n\n    /// Validate the model and return a metric (higher is better).\n    fn validate(&self, dataset: DatasetView) -> Result<Self::Metric, TuningError>;\n}\n\n// ----------------------------- Data Contracts --------------------------------\n/// A lightweight view over a data split.\n///\n/// NOTE: In the real platform this is a zero-copy view into an Arrow Flight\n/// stream.  For brevity, we merely keep a string ID here.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug)]\npub struct DatasetView {\n    pub id: String,\n}\n\n// ------------------------------ Experiment I/O -------------------------------\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct TrialRecord<M: Trainable> {\n    pub params: M::HyperParams,\n    pub metric: M::Metric,\n    pub duration_ms: u128,\n}\n\n/// Event emitted by the tuning engine.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone)]\npub enum ExperimentEvent<M: Trainable> {\n    TrialStarted(M::HyperParams),\n    TrialCompleted(TrialRecord<M>),\n    TuningFinished(Option<TrialRecord<M>>),\n}\n\n/// Observer interface (pull-based is also supported in other modules).\npub trait ExperimentObserver<M: Trainable>: Send + Sync {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: ExperimentEvent<M>);\n}\n\n/// Thread-safe, in-memory observer used in tests and local runs.\n#[derive(Default)]\npub struct InMemoryObserver<M: Trainable> {\n    events: Arc<Mutex<Vec<ExperimentEvent<M>>>>,\n}\nimpl<M: Trainable> InMemoryObserver<M> {\n    pub fn events(&self) -> Vec<ExperimentEvent<M>> {\n        self.events.lock().unwrap().clone()\n    }\n}\nimpl<M: Trainable> ExperimentObserver<M> for InMemoryObserver<M> {\n    fn on_event(&self, event: ExperimentEvent<M>) {\n        self.events.lock().unwrap().push(event);\n    }\n}\n\n// ----------------------------- Tuner Strategy --------------------------------\npub trait TunerStrategy<M: Trainable>: Send + Sync {\n    /// Run the tuning loop and return the best trial record (if any).\n    fn tune(\n        &self,\n        space: HyperParamSpace<M>,\n        dataset: DatasetView,\n        observers: &[Arc<dyn ExperimentObserver<M>>],\n    ) -> Result<Option<TrialRecord<M>>, TuningError>;\n}\n\n/// Hyper-parameter search space.\n///\n/// In the real system this would allow conditional spaces, distributions,\n/// nested structures, etc.  Here we simply map parameter names to candidate\n/// categorical values.\n#[derive(Clone)]\npub struct HyperParamSpace<M: Trainable> {\n    choices: HashMap<String, Vec<serde_json::Value>>,\n    _phantom: std::marker::PhantomData<M>,\n}\nimpl<M: Trainable> HyperParamSpace<M> {\n    pub fn new() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            choices: HashMap::new(),\n            _phantom: std::marker::PhantomData,\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn add_choice<T: Serialize>(&mut self, name: &str, values: Vec<T>) {\n        self.choices.insert(\n            name.to_owned(),\n            values\n                .into_iter()\n                .map(|v| serde_json::to_value(v).expect(\"serialise hyper-param\"))\n                .collect(),\n        );\n    }\n\n    fn enumerate_grid(&self) -> Vec<M::HyperParams> {\n        // A na\u00efve Cartesian product enumerator. Usually replaced by an iterator\n        // that yields lazily to avoid combinatorial explosion.\n        let mut param_maps: Vec<HashMap<String, serde_json::Value>> = vec![HashMap::new()];\n\n        for (key, choices) in &self.choices {\n            let mut next_maps = Vec::new();\n            for choice in choices {\n                for base in &param_maps {\n                    let mut map = base.clone();\n                    map.insert(key.clone(), choice.clone());\n                    next_maps.push(map);\n                }\n            }\n            param_maps = next_maps;\n        }\n\n        param_maps\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|map| serde_json::from_value::<M::HyperParams>(serde_json::Value::Object(\n                map.into_iter().collect(),\n            ))\n            .expect(\"convert to HyperParams\"))\n            .collect()\n    }\n\n    fn pick_random(&self, rng: &mut StdRng) -> Option<M::HyperParams> {\n        let mut map = HashMap::<String, serde_json::Value>::new();\n        for (k, choices) in &self.choices {\n            let choice = choices.iter().choose(rng)?;\n            map.insert(k.clone(), choice.clone());\n        }\n        serde_json::from_value(serde_json::Value::Object(map.into_iter().collect())).ok()\n    }\n}\n\n// --------------------- Concrete Strategies ----------------------------------\npub struct GridSearchTuner;\nimpl<M: Trainable> TunerStrategy<M> for GridSearchTuner {\n    fn tune(\n        &self,\n        space: HyperParamSpace<M>,\n        dataset: DatasetView,\n        observers: &[Arc<dyn ExperimentObserver<M>>],\n    ) -> Result<Option<TrialRecord<M>>, TuningError> {\n        let mut best: Option<TrialRecord<M>> = None;\n\n        for params in space.enumerate_grid() {\n            notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TrialStarted(params.clone()));\n            let start = Instant::now();\n\n            let mut model = M::new(&params)?;\n            model.train(dataset.clone())?;\n            let metric = model.validate(dataset.clone())?;\n\n            let record = TrialRecord {\n                params: params.clone(),\n                metric,\n                duration_ms: start.elapsed().as_millis(),\n            };\n            notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TrialCompleted(record.clone()));\n\n            if best.as_ref().map(|b| metric > b.metric).unwrap_or(true) {\n                best = Some(record);\n            }\n        }\n\n        notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TuningFinished(best.clone()));\n        Ok(best)\n    }\n}\n\npub struct RandomSearchTuner {\n    trials: usize,\n    seed: u64,\n}\nimpl RandomSearchTuner {\n    pub fn new(trials: usize, seed: u64) -> Self {\n        Self { trials, seed }\n    }\n}\nimpl<M: Trainable> TunerStrategy<M> for RandomSearchTuner {\n    fn tune(\n        &self,\n        space: HyperParamSpace<M>,\n        dataset: DatasetView,\n        observers: &[Arc<dyn ExperimentObserver<M>>],\n    ) -> Result<Option<TrialRecord<M>>, TuningError> {\n        let mut best: Option<TrialRecord<M>> = None;\n        let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(self.seed);\n\n        for _ in 0..self.trials {\n            let params = match space.pick_random(&mut rng) {\n                Some(p) => p,\n                None => return Err(TuningError::InvalidSpace(\"space is empty\".into())),\n            };\n\n            notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TrialStarted(params.clone()));\n            let start = Instant::now();\n\n            let mut model = M::new(&params)?;\n            model.train(dataset.clone())?;\n            let metric = model.validate(dataset.clone())?;\n\n            let record = TrialRecord {\n                params: params.clone(),\n                metric,\n                duration_ms: start.elapsed().as_millis(),\n            };\n            notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TrialCompleted(record.clone()));\n\n            if best.as_ref().map(|b| metric > b.metric).unwrap_or(true) {\n                best = Some(record);\n            }\n        }\n\n        notify(observers, ExperimentEvent::TuningFinished(best.clone()));\n        Ok(best)\n    }\n}\n\n// ------------------------------ Factory --------------------------------------\n#[derive(Clone, Copy)]\npub enum TunerKind {\n    Grid,\n    Random { trials: usize, seed: u64 },\n}\n\npub struct TunerFactory;\nimpl TunerFactory {\n    pub fn create<M: Trainable>(kind: TunerKind) -> Box<dyn TunerStrategy<M>> {\n        match kind {\n            TunerKind::Grid => Box::new(GridSearchTuner),\n            TunerKind::Random { trials, seed } => Box::new(RandomSearchTuner::new(trials, seed)),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// ------------------------- Pipeline Orchestrator -----------------------------\npub async fn run_hyperparameter_tuning<M>(\n    kind: TunerKind,\n    space: HyperParamSpace<M>,\n    dataset: DatasetView,\n    observers: Vec<Arc<dyn ExperimentObserver<M>>>,\n) -> Result<Option<TrialRecord<M>>, TuningError>\nwhere\n    M: Trainable,\n{\n    let tuner = TunerFactory::create(kind);\n\n    // Offload to a blocking thread pool to avoid holding up async reactors.\n    let result = task::spawn_blocking(move || tuner.tune(space, dataset, &observers)).await?;\n\n    result\n}\n\n// ----------------------------- Helper Functions ------------------------------\nfn notify<M: Trainable>(observers: &[Arc<dyn ExperimentObserver<M>>], event: ExperimentEvent<M>) {\n    for obs in observers {\n        obs.on_event(event.clone());\n    }\n}\n\n// ------------------------ Mock Implementation (tests) -----------------------\n//! In real life, each domain model implements `Trainable` in its own crate.\n//! Below is a synthetic model so `cargo test` compiles without extra deps.\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n    // Dummy model that tries to maximise x \u2011 y.\n    #[derive(Debug)]\n    struct DummyModel {\n        x: i32,\n        y: i32,\n    }\n\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n    struct DummyParams {\n        x: i32,\n        y: i32,\n    }\n\n    impl Trainable for DummyModel {\n        type HyperParams = DummyParams;\n        type Metric = i32;\n\n        fn new(params: &Self::HyperParams) -> Result<Self, TuningError> {\n            Ok(Self {\n                x: params.x,\n                y: params.y,\n            })\n        }\n\n        fn train(&mut self, _dataset: DatasetView) -> Result<(), TuningError> {\n            Ok(())\n        }\n\n        fn validate(&self, _dataset: DatasetView) -> Result<Self::Metric, TuningError> {\n            Ok(self.x - self.y)\n        }\n    }\n\n    fn sample_space() -> HyperParamSpace<DummyModel> {\n        let mut space = HyperParamSpace::<DummyModel>::new();\n        space.add_choice(\"x\", vec![1, 2, 3]);\n        space.add_choice(\"y\", vec![0, 1, 2]);\n        space\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_grid_search_finds_best() {\n        let dataset = DatasetView { id: \"dummy\".into() };\n        let obs = Arc::new(InMemoryObserver::<DummyModel>::default());\n\n        let best = run_hyperparameter_tuning(\n            TunerKind::Grid,\n            sample_space(),\n            dataset,\n            vec![obs.clone()],\n        )\n        .await\n        .unwrap()\n        .unwrap();\n\n        assert_eq!(best.metric, 3); // (x=3, y=0) => 3\n        assert!(!obs.events().is_empty());\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn test_random_search_executes() {\n        let dataset = DatasetView { id: \"dummy\".into() };\n        let obs = Arc::new(InMemoryObserver::<DummyModel>::default());\n\n        let _ = run_hyperparameter_tuning(\n            TunerKind::Random {\n                trials: 5,\n                seed: 42,\n            },\n            sample_space(),\n            dataset,\n            vec![obs.clone()],\n        )\n        .await\n        .unwrap();\n\n        assert_eq!(obs.events().len(), 5 * 2 + 1); // start + complete per trial + finished\n    }\n}\n```",

    "content": "//! Generic utilities commonly used across VisuTility Orchestrator.\n//!\n//! The abstractions in this module are intentionally framework-agnostic:\n//! they do not depend on any particular CV/ML crate and can therefore be\n//! shared by every layer (Ingress, Data-Ops, Feature-Ops, \u2026).\n//!\n//! All functions are `#[inline]` where it makes sense to do so, and\n//! significant branches are annotated with `#[cold]` to let the optimizer\n//! keep hot-paths small.\n\nuse std::{\n    fmt,\n    fs::File,\n    io::Read,\n    path::{Path, PathBuf},\n    sync::atomic::{AtomicUsize, Ordering},\n    time::{Duration, Instant},\n};\n\nuse anyhow::{anyhow, Context, Result};\nuse once_cell::sync::Lazy;\nuse parking_lot::RwLock;\nuse serde::de::DeserializeOwned;\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\nuse tracing::{debug, error, info, instrument};\n\n/// VisuTility's generic error type for utility-layer operations.\n///\n/// We prefer using [`anyhow::Error`] at the top-level application\n/// boundary to allow for heterogeneous sources, but within the\n/// utility layer we capture the most common failure categories so that\n/// callers can still pattern-match when they need to.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum UtilError {\n    #[error(\"I/O error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"configuration not found at path `{0}`\")]\n    ConfigNotFound(PathBuf),\n\n    #[error(\"task failed: {0}\")]\n    TaskFailed(String),\n}\n\n/// Generic wrapper around an [`Instant`] which logs the elapsed time at\n/// **drop**.  The measurement is therefore *scoped*; as soon as the guard\n/// goes out of scope, latency is emitted through the `tracing` facade.\n///\n/// ```no_run\n/// use visu_tility_utils::ScopedTimer;\n/// let _g = ScopedTimer::new(\"heavy_initialisation\");\n/// // \u2026 some expensive code \u2026\n\u2014 guard drops here and we get a log line with\n//   the elapsed time\n/// ```\npub struct ScopedTimer<'a> {\n    started: Instant,\n    label: &'a str,\n}\n\nimpl<'a> ScopedTimer<'a> {\n    /// Begin measuring elapsed time for the supplied label.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn new(label: &'a str) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            started: Instant::now(),\n            label,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Stop the timer and return the [`Duration`] since creation without\n    /// logging. This allows manual control when automatic logging at `drop`\n    /// is not desired.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn stop(self) -> Duration {\n        Instant::now() - self.started\n    }\n}\n\nimpl<'a> Drop for ScopedTimer<'a> {\n    fn drop(&mut self) {\n        let elapsed = Instant::now() - self.started;\n        info!(\n            label = %self.label,\n            ms = %elapsed.as_millis(),\n            \"ScopedTimer finished\"\n        );\n        METRICS\n            .write()\n            .record_duration(self.label, elapsed.as_secs_f64());\n    }\n}\n\n/// Global metrics collector with *zero* external dependencies.  This is\n/// intentionally minimal because higher layers might choose to forward these\n/// numbers to Prometheus, StatsD, or another monitoring backend.\n///\n/// Internally it stores *exponential moving averages* so that it can be used\n/// in hot-paths without unbounded memory growth.\npub struct Metrics {\n    /// Moving average of durations (seconds) per label.\n    durations: std::collections::HashMap<String, f64>,\n    /// EWMA smoothing factor in `[0,1]`.\n    alpha: f64,\n}\n\nimpl Metrics {\n    fn new(alpha: f64) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            durations: std::collections::HashMap::new(),\n            alpha,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Record a latency sample under `label`.\n    pub fn record_duration(&mut self, label: impl Into<String>, secs: f64) {\n        let label = label.into();\n        let entry = self.durations.entry(label).or_insert(secs);\n        // EWMA: v_t = alpha * x_t + (1-alpha) * v_{t-1}\n        *entry = self.alpha * secs + (1.0 - self.alpha) * *entry;\n    }\n\n    /// Return the current EWMA for `label`, if any.\n    pub fn duration_avg(&self, label: &str) -> Option<f64> {\n        self.durations.get(label).copied()\n    }\n}\n\n/// Static metrics instance; tweak the smoothing factor as needed.\n/// We protect it with a *fair* RwLock to allow many concurrent readers.\nstatic METRICS: Lazy<RwLock<Metrics>> = Lazy::new(|| RwLock::new(Metrics::new(0.20)));\n\n/// Typed representation of the global **application config**.\n///\n/// This is intentionally limited to fields that the utility layer needs\n/// to know about; higher layers maintain their own extensions.\n///\n/// Because config files are versioned in the Model Registry, we include a\n/// `schema_version` field to prevent silent breakage when the expected\n/// structure changes.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct AppConfig {\n    pub schema_version: u16,\n    pub experiment_tracking_uri: Option<String>,\n    pub model_registry_uri: Option<String>,\n    pub default_retry: RetryConfig,\n    /// Additional arbitrary key/value flavour that can be stored alongside\n    /// the canonical config.  Can be abused for feature flags, etc.\n    #[serde(default)]\n    pub user: std::collections::HashMap<String, serde_json::Value>,\n}\n\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct RetryConfig {\n    pub max_attempts: usize,\n    pub backoff_millis: u64,\n}\n\nimpl Default for RetryConfig {\n    fn default() -> Self {\n        Self {\n            max_attempts: 3,\n            backoff_millis: 500,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Maximum size (bytes) that we allow a configuration file to have before\n/// we refuse to load it.  Protects against accidental loading of huge blobs.\nconst MAX_CONFIG_SIZE: usize = 256 * 1024; // 256 KiB\n\n/// Load and parse application configuration **once** at start-up.\n///\n/// The file format is auto-detected based on extension (`.yaml`/`.yml` or\n/// `.json`).  The resulting struct is cached in a global `Lazy`.\n///\n/// Example:\n/// ```no_run\n/// let cfg = visu_tility_utils::config();\n/// println!(\"Schema v{} loaded\", cfg.schema_version);\n/// ```\nfn read_config_from_disk(path: &Path) -> Result<AppConfig> {\n    if !path.exists() {\n        return Err(UtilError::ConfigNotFound(path.into()).into());\n    }\n\n    let mut file =\n        File::open(path).with_context(|| format!(\"opening configuration file `{}`\", path.display()))?;\n\n    let mut buf = Vec::new();\n    file.read_to_end(&mut buf)\n        .with_context(|| format!(\"reading configuration file `{}`\", path.display()))?;\n\n    if buf.len() > MAX_CONFIG_SIZE {\n        return Err(anyhow!(\n            \"configuration file `{}` larger than {} KiB\",\n            path.display(),\n            MAX_CONFIG_SIZE / 1024\n        ));\n    }\n\n    let cfg = match path.extension().and_then(|s| s.to_str()) {\n        Some(\"yaml\") | Some(\"yml\") => serde_yaml::from_slice(&buf)?,\n        Some(\"json\") => serde_json::from_slice(&buf)?,\n        other => {\n            return Err(anyhow!(\n                \"unsupported configuration extension {:?} for `{}`\",\n                other,\n                path.display()\n            ))\n        }\n    };\n\n    Ok(cfg)\n}\n\n/// Discover the config path in the following order:\n///\n/// 1. Explicit argument via `VISU_CONFIG` environment variable.\n/// 2. `${CWD}/visu_config.yaml`\n/// 3. `${CWD}/visu_config.json`\nfn auto_discover_config() -> Option<PathBuf> {\n    if let Ok(path) = std::env::var(\"VISU_CONFIG\") {\n        return Some(PathBuf::from(path));\n    }\n\n    const CANDIDATES: &[&str] = &[\"visu_config.yaml\", \"visu_config.yml\", \"visu_config.json\"];\n    for c in CANDIDATES {\n        let p = PathBuf::from(c);\n        if p.exists() {\n            return Some(p);\n        }\n    }\n    None\n}\n\n/// Global application configuration singleton.\nstatic CONFIG: Lazy<AppConfig> = Lazy::new(|| {\n    let path = auto_discover_config()\n        .unwrap_or_else(|| PathBuf::from(\"visu_config.yaml\")); // fallback for nicer error msg\n    match read_config_from_disk(&path) {\n        Ok(cfg) => {\n            info!(\n                file = %path.display(),\n                version = cfg.schema_version,\n                \"configuration file loaded\"\n            );\n            cfg\n        }\n        Err(e) => {\n            error!(\n                file = %path.display(),\n                error = %e,\n                \"failed to load configuration; using built-in defaults\"\n            );\n            // Fallback\n            AppConfig {\n                schema_version: 0,\n                experiment_tracking_uri: None,\n                model_registry_uri: None,\n                default_retry: RetryConfig::default(),\n                user: Default::default(),\n            }\n        }\n    }\n});\n\n/// Access the application-wide [`AppConfig`].\n#[inline]\npub fn config() -> &'static AppConfig {\n    &CONFIG\n}\n\n/// Generic exponential *back-off* / *retry* helper.\n///\n/// The provided closure is executed until it either succeeds or\n/// max_attempts have been reached.\n///\n/// Usage:\n/// ```ignore\n/// use visu_tility_utils::retry;\n///\n/// let result = retry(\n///     &config().default_retry,\n///     || {\n///         // call external dependency that might fail\n///         some_unstable_operation()\n///     });\n/// ```\npub fn retry<F, T, E>(cfg: &RetryConfig, mut f: F) -> Result<T, E>\nwhere\n    F: FnMut() -> Result<T, E>,\n{\n    let mut attempt = 0;\n    loop {\n        match f() {\n            Ok(v) => return Ok(v),\n            Err(e) if attempt + 1 == cfg.max_attempts => return Err(e),\n            Err(_e) => {\n                attempt += 1;\n                std::thread::sleep(Duration::from_millis(cfg.backoff_millis));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Simple **ID generator** that hands out monotonically increasing\n/// identifiers from a global counter.\n///\n/// This is useful when datasets or intermediate artefacts need a\n/// transaction-like handle but heavyweight UUIDs are overkill.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]\npub struct Id(u64);\n\n// global counter\nstatic COUNTER: AtomicUsize = AtomicUsize::new(1);\n\nimpl Id {\n    /// Allocate a fresh id.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn fresh() -> Self {\n        let n = COUNTER.fetch_add(1, Ordering::Relaxed);\n        Id(n as u64)\n    }\n\n    /// Return the underlying integer.\n    #[inline]\n    pub fn as_u64(self) -> u64 {\n        self.0\n    }\n}\n\nimpl fmt::Display for Id {\n    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {\n        self.0.fmt(f)\n    }\n}\n\n/// **Observer pattern**: runtime event bus.\n//\n/// Very light-weight publisher/subscriber abstraction built on top of\n/// [`crossbeam_channel`].  Since layers of the Orchestrator run in\n/// different scheduling contexts we cannot rely on *any* runtime; a\n/// channel-based design has zero dependencies on async executors.\npub mod event_bus {\n    use super::*;\n    use crossbeam_channel::{unbounded, Receiver, Sender};\n\n    /// Event types that travel on the bus.  This enum grows over time as new\n    /// features make use of the bus; by keeping it located in a *utility*\n    /// crate we avoid circular dependencies.\n    #[derive(Debug, Clone)]\n    pub enum Event {\n        HyperparameterTuningStarted { experiment_id: Id },\n        HyperparameterTuningFinished { experiment_id: Id },\n        ModelRegistered {\n            name: String,\n            version: String,\n            metadata: std::collections::HashMap<String, String>,\n        },\n        ModelDriftDetected {\n            model: String,\n            magnitude: f32,\n            timestamp: chrono::DateTime<chrono::Utc>,\n        },\n        Custom(String, serde_json::Value),\n    }\n\n    /// Handle required for publishing events.\n    #[derive(Clone)]\n    pub struct Publisher {\n        tx: Sender<Event>,\n    }\n\n    impl Publisher {\n        /// Publish an event; errors are logged but otherwise ignored since the\n        /// system should remain functional even when no-one is listening.\n        pub fn publish(&self, evt: Event) {\n            if let Err(e) = self.tx.send(evt.clone()) {\n                debug!(error = ?e, event = ?evt, \"failed to publish event\");\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// A stream of events.\n    pub type Subscription = Receiver<Event>;\n\n    /// Construct a **single** global bus so that layers can obtain\n    /// cheap clones of the `Publisher` without having to pass them around.\n    static BUS: Lazy<(Publisher, Subscription)> = Lazy::new(|| {\n        let (tx, rx) = unbounded::<Event>();\n        (Publisher { tx }, rx)\n    });\n\n    /// Return a handle for *publishing* events.\n    pub fn publisher() -> Publisher {\n        BUS.0.clone()\n    }\n\n    /// Subscribe to events.  Every caller receives a *clone* of the receiver\n    /// which means all subscribers see *all* events (fan-out).\n    pub fn subscribe() -> Subscription {\n        BUS.1.clone()\n    }\n}\n\n/// A small proc-macro-like helper (implemented as declarative macro to avoid meta\n/// crate) for scoped timing.\n///\n/// ```\n/// visu_tility_utils::scope_time!(\"fancy_stage\", {\n///     expensive();\n/// });\n/// ```\n#[macro_export]\nmacro_rules! scope_time {\n    ($label:expr, $block:block) => {{\n        let _g = $crate::ScopedTimer::new($label);\n        $block\n    }};\n}\n\n/// Tests live inside the same file so that the utils crate remains\n/// a **single** compilation unit.  This is important for global singletons\n/// (`Lazy`) which must not be duplicated across multiple crates.\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn id_monotonicity() {\n        let a = Id::fresh();\n        let b = Id::fresh();\n        assert!(b.as_u64() > a.as_u64());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn retry_succeeds_eventually() {\n        let cfg = RetryConfig {\n            max_attempts: 5,\n            backoff_millis: 1,\n        };\n        let mut n = 0;\n        let res: Result<usize, usize> = retry(&cfg, || {\n            if n < 3 {\n                n += 1;\n                Err(n)\n            } else {\n                Ok(n)\n            }\n        });\n        assert_eq!(res.unwrap(), 3);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn metrics_ewma() {\n        METRICS.write().record_duration(\"foo\", 1.0);\n        METRICS.write().record_duration(\"foo\", 1.0);\n        let avg = METRICS.read().duration_avg(\"foo\").unwrap();\n        assert!(avg > 0.0 && avg <= 1.0);\n    }\n}",

    "content": "```rust\n//! Hyper-parameter Tuning Engine\n//!\n//! This module implements a Strategy-Pattern\u2013based hyper-parameter tuning\n//! engine that can be plugged into any stage of the VisuTility Orchestrator\n//! pipeline. The engine provides:\n//!   \u2022 A generic [`Tuner`] fa\u00e7ade that coordinates trial execution\n//!   \u2022 Pluggable tuning strategies (e.g. Grid, Random, Bayesian)\n//!   \u2022 Observer hooks for experiment tracking & early-stopping\n//!\n//! The code purposefully avoids project-specific dependencies so it can be\n//! re-used by other crates within the workspace. All heavy lifting (model\n//! compilation, dataset loading, etc.) is delegated to an [`Objective`]\n//! implementation supplied by the caller.\n\nuse std::collections::HashMap;\nuse std::fmt;\nuse std::sync::{Arc, Mutex};\nuse std::time::{Duration, Instant};\n\nuse crossbeam_channel::{unbounded, Receiver, Sender};\nuse rand::distributions::{Distribution, Uniform};\nuse rand::{rngs::StdRng, SeedableRng};\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\nuse thiserror::Error;\n\n/// Generic error type for the tuning engine.\n#[derive(Debug, Error)]\npub enum TuningError {\n    #[error(\"objective function failed: {0}\")]\n    ObjectiveFailed(String),\n\n    #[error(\"invalid parameter space definition: {0}\")]\n    InvalidParameter(String),\n\n    #[error(\"I/O error: {0}\")]\n    Io(#[from] std::io::Error),\n\n    #[error(\"serialization error: {0}\")]\n    Serde(#[from] serde_json::Error),\n}\n\n/// Domain of a single hyper-parameter.\n///\n/// The enum is intentionally limited to float & discrete types to keep the\n/// sample code concise. In production you may want Boolean, Categorical, etc.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub enum ParameterDomain {\n    Continuous { low: f64, high: f64 },\n    Discrete(Vec<f64>),\n}\n\nimpl ParameterDomain {\n    /// Sample a value from the domain.\n    fn sample<R: rand::Rng>(&self, rng: &mut R) -> f64 {\n        match self {\n            ParameterDomain::Continuous { low, high } => {\n                let distr = Uniform::new(*low, *high);\n                distr.sample(rng)\n            }\n            ParameterDomain::Discrete(values) => {\n                let idx = rng.gen_range(0..values.len());\n                values[idx]\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Iterate over all discrete points when applicable.\n    fn iter(&self) -> Option<impl Iterator<Item = f64> + '_> {\n        match self {\n            ParameterDomain::Discrete(values) => Some(values.iter().copied()),\n            _ => None,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Collection of named domains.\npub type ParameterSpace = HashMap<String, ParameterDomain>;\n\n/// Concrete set of hyper-parameters for a single trial.\npub type HyperParams = HashMap<String, f64>;\n\n/// Result produced by a single trial.\n#[derive(Clone, Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct TrialResult {\n    pub params: HyperParams,\n    pub score: f64,\n    pub duration: Duration,\n}\n\n/// Contract for objective evaluation.\n///\n/// Implementors should train a model (or a down-scaled proxy) and return the\n/// metric that the tuning process must optimize (higher is better).\npub trait Objective: Send + Sync + 'static {\n    fn evaluate(&self, params: &HyperParams) -> Result<f64, TuningError>;\n}\n\n/// Observer pattern for side-effects such as logging, experiment tracking,\n/// early stopping, etc.\npub trait TuningObserver: Send + Sync {\n    fn on_trial_completed(&self, result: &TrialResult);\n}\n\n/// Strategy pattern for search algorithms.\npub trait TuningStrategy: Send + Sync {\n    fn next_parameters(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams>;\n    fn register_result(&mut self, _result: &TrialResult) {}\n}\n\n/// Grid Search implementation.\n///\n/// Explores the cartesian product of every discrete domain, *ignoring*\n/// continuous ones. If the user provides only continuous spaces, the grid is\n/// empty and `next_parameters` will always return `None`.\npub struct GridSearch {\n    grid: Vec<HyperParams>,\n    cursor: usize,\n}\n\nimpl GridSearch {\n    pub fn new(space: &ParameterSpace) -> Self {\n        let mut grid: Vec<HyperParams> = vec![HyperParams::new()];\n        for (name, domain) in space {\n            if let Some(iter) = domain.iter() {\n                let mut next_grid = Vec::with_capacity(grid.len() * 4);\n                for existing in &grid {\n                    for value in iter.clone() {\n                        let mut params = existing.clone();\n                        params.insert(name.clone(), value);\n                        next_grid.push(params);\n                    }\n                }\n                grid = next_grid;\n            }\n        }\n        Self { grid, cursor: 0 }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TuningStrategy for GridSearch {\n    fn next_parameters(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.cursor < self.grid.len() {\n            let params = self.grid[self.cursor].clone();\n            self.cursor += 1;\n            Some(params)\n        } else {\n            None\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Random Search implementation using a seeded PRNG.\npub struct RandomSearch {\n    space: ParameterSpace,\n    rng: StdRng,\n    max_trials: usize,\n    generated: usize,\n}\n\nimpl RandomSearch {\n    pub fn new(space: ParameterSpace, max_trials: usize, seed: u64) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            space,\n            rng: StdRng::seed_from_u64(seed),\n            max_trials,\n            generated: 0,\n        }\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TuningStrategy for RandomSearch {\n    fn next_parameters(&mut self) -> Option<HyperParams> {\n        if self.generated >= self.max_trials {\n            return None;\n        }\n        let mut params = HyperParams::with_capacity(self.space.len());\n        for (name, domain) in &self.space {\n            params.insert(name.clone(), domain.sample(&mut self.rng));\n        }\n        self.generated += 1;\n        Some(params)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Thread-safe experiment tracker that writes each trial to a JSON Lines file.\n/// The implementation is intentionally simple and can be replaced by something\n/// like MLflow, Weights & Biases, or a SQL database.\npub struct JsonlTracker {\n    file: Arc<Mutex<std::fs::File>>,\n}\n\nimpl JsonlTracker {\n    pub fn new(path: impl AsRef<std::path::Path>) -> Result<Self, TuningError> {\n        let file = std::fs::OpenOptions::new()\n            .create(true)\n            .append(true)\n            .open(path)?;\n        Ok(Self {\n            file: Arc::new(Mutex::new(file)),\n        })\n    }\n}\n\nimpl TuningObserver for JsonlTracker {\n    fn on_trial_completed(&self, result: &TrialResult) {\n        if let Ok(serialized) = serde_json::to_string(result) {\n            if let Ok(mut file) = self.file.lock() {\n                // Ignore I/O errors so tuning can proceed.\n                let _ = writeln!(file, \"{}\", serialized);\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Central fa\u00e7ade that orchestrates strategy, observers and objective.\npub struct Tuner<S: TuningStrategy> {\n    strategy: S,\n    objective: Arc<dyn Objective>,\n    observers: Vec<Arc<dyn TuningObserver>>,\n    tx: Sender<TrialResult>,\n    rx: Receiver<TrialResult>,\n}\n\nimpl<S: TuningStrategy> Tuner<S> {\n    pub fn builder(strategy: S, objective: Arc<dyn Objective>) -> TunerBuilder<S> {\n        TunerBuilder::new(strategy, objective)\n    }\n\n    fn new(strategy: S, objective: Arc<dyn Objective>, observers: Vec<Arc<dyn TuningObserver>>) -> Self {\n        let (tx, rx) = unbounded();\n        Self {\n            strategy,\n            objective,\n            observers,\n            tx,\n            rx,\n        }\n    }\n\n    /// Drives the tuning loop until the strategy is exhausted or an error\n    /// occurs. Returns the best trial encountered.\n    pub fn run(&mut self) -> Result<TrialResult, TuningError> {\n        let mut best: Option<TrialResult> = None;\n\n        // Spawn a simple worker thread pool (1 thread / logical core).\n        let n_workers = num_cpus::get();\n        let mut handles = Vec::with_capacity(n_workers);\n        for _ in 0..n_workers {\n            let tx = self.tx.clone();\n            let objective = self.objective.clone();\n            let mut local_strategy = &mut self.strategy as *mut S; // raw ptr to share across threads\n            handles.push(std::thread::spawn(move || loop {\n                // SAFETY: Exclusive access is guaranteed by the global lock below.\n                let params = {\n                    // Strategy access is synchronized via a global mutex.\n                    static STRATEGY_LOCK: once_cell::sync::Lazy<Mutex<()>> =\n                        once_cell::sync::Lazy::new(|| Mutex::new(()));\n                    let _guard = STRATEGY_LOCK.lock().unwrap();\n                    // Mutable borrow of the strategy behind the raw pointer.\n                    unsafe { &mut *local_strategy }.next_parameters()\n                };\n\n                let params = match params {\n                    Some(p) => p,\n                    None => break, // no more work\n                };\n\n                let time_start = Instant::now();\n                let score = match objective.evaluate(&params) {\n                    Ok(s) => s,\n                    Err(e) => {\n                        let _ = tx.send(TrialResult {\n                            params,\n                            score: f64::NAN,\n                            duration: time_start.elapsed(),\n                        });\n                        eprintln!(\"Objective failed: {e}\");\n                        continue;\n                    }\n                };\n\n                let result = TrialResult {\n                    params,\n                    score,\n                    duration: time_start.elapsed(),\n                };\n                let _ = tx.send(result);\n            }));\n        }\n\n        drop(self.tx); // Close senders when workers finish.\n\n        // Collect results & notify observers.\n        for trial in &self.rx {\n            self.strategy.register_result(&trial);\n            for obs in &self.observers {\n                obs.on_trial_completed(&trial);\n            }\n            if best.as_ref().map_or(true, |b| trial.score > b.score) {\n                best = Some(trial);\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Wait for threads to finish.\n        for h in handles {\n            let _ = h.join();\n        }\n\n        best.ok_or_else(|| TuningError::InvalidParameter(\"No trials executed\".into()))\n    }\n}\n\n/// Builder for [`Tuner`] allowing ergonomic configuration.\npub struct TunerBuilder<S: TuningStrategy> {\n    strategy: S,\n    objective: Arc<dyn Objective>,\n    observers: Vec<Arc<dyn TuningObserver>>,\n}\n\nimpl<S: TuningStrategy> TunerBuilder<S> {\n    fn new(strategy: S, objective: Arc<dyn Objective>) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            strategy,\n            objective,\n            observers: Vec::new(),\n        }\n    }\n\n    pub fn with_observer(mut self, observer: Arc<dyn TuningObserver>) -> Self {\n        self.observers.push(observer);\n        self\n    }\n\n    pub fn build(self) -> Tuner<S> {\n        Tuner::new(self.strategy, self.objective, self.observers)\n    }\n}\n\n/// Example objective for demonstration purposes only.\n///\n/// The objective is a noisy parabola whose global maximum is\n/// near x=0.42, y=0.69. This allows the tuner to finish quickly.\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    struct DummyObjective;\n\n    impl Objective for DummyObjective {\n        fn evaluate(&self, params: &HyperParams) -> Result<f64, TuningError> {\n            let x = params.get(\"x\").copied().unwrap_or(0.0);\n            let y = params.get(\"y\").copied().unwrap_or(0.0);\n            // simple 2-D inverted paraboloid + random noise\n            let value = -(x - 0.42).powi(2) - (y - 0.69).powi(2) + 1.0\n                + rand::random::<f64>() * 0.01;\n            Ok(value)\n        }\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn random_search_converges() -> Result<(), TuningError> {\n        let mut space = ParameterSpace::new();\n        space.insert(\"x\".into(), ParameterDomain::Continuous { low: 0.0, high: 1.0 });\n        space.insert(\"y\".into(), ParameterDomain::Continuous { low: 0.0, high: 1.0 });\n\n        let strategy = RandomSearch::new(space, 1_000, 42);\n        let objective = Arc::new(DummyObjective);\n        let tracker = Arc::new(JsonlTracker::new(std::env::temp_dir().join(\"trials.jsonl\"))?);\n\n        let mut tuner = Tuner::builder(strategy, objective)\n            .with_observer(tracker)\n            .build();\n\n        let best = tuner.run()?;\n        assert!(best.score > 0.95, \"best score too low: {}\", best.score);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn grid_search_enumerates_discrete() -> Result<(), TuningError> {\n        let mut space = ParameterSpace::new();\n        space.insert(\"x\".into(), ParameterDomain::Discrete(vec![0.0, 0.5, 1.0]));\n        space.insert(\"y\".into(), ParameterDomain::Discrete(vec![0.0, 1.0]));\n\n        let strategy = GridSearch::new(&space);\n        let objective = Arc::new(DummyObjective);\n\n        let mut tuner = Tuner::builder(strategy, objective).build();\n        let best = tuner.run()?;\n        assert!(best.score > 0.9);\n        Ok(())\n    }\n}\n```",
